FUNCTIONS\n\nThis section documents detailed requirements for subfunctions\nidentified as being common to two or more navigation principal\nfunctions or their major subfunctions. These models are to be used in the\norbiter state propagation whenever the IU-sensed accelerations\t\n\n.^\n\nare below a given threshold level. Propagation or prediction of\nthe target vehicle\'s state shall use the gravitational and drag\nmodels\n\ni\nThe currently functioning propagator and a predictor may need\ndifferent models at the same time. It is therefore necessary that\nthe execution of the acceleration calculations be protected from\ninterruption by other users.\n\nFor the computation of the accelerations due to the Earth\'s gravity,\noptions shall be.provided to include terms derived from various\ndegree and order gravitational potential models. Input flags-GMD\nand GMO shall be set by the user to specify, respectively, the degree\nand order, of the;gravitationa1 potent\'ia model to be used. Similarly,\nan input flag, DM, shall be set by the user to indicate whether\nor not to model drag. The covariance matrix\nis propagated by utilizing the state transition matrix. Additive process noise is incorporated to account for unmodeled\nstate and dynamic errors.\n\nA.\n\nDetailed Requirements. A 9 by 9 covariance matrix shall\n\nbe propagated with the navigation principal function. This\ncovariance matrix defines the uncertainty in the state vector,\nwhich consists of position and velocity of the orbiter and\nunmodeled accelerations. The method of propagation is descri bed in Section 4.2.2.\n\nB.\n\nInterface Requirements The input and output data are shown\n\nin Tables 4.3.1.4-1 and 4.3.1.4-2,\n\nC.\n\nProcessing Requirements. This subfunction will be called\n\nafter the IMU sensor data have been read and after the state\npropagation subfunction has been executed\nagation\n\nD.\n\nConstraints Prestored data are to be used for initiali-\n\nzation. The propagated covariance matrix must remain symmetric.\n\nE.\n\ni\n\n_^\t\n\nSupplementary Information. Detailed Requirements\nThe rendezvous sensor measurement select\'i`on subfunction\nshall provide\n\na\n\ncapability for determining when star\n\ntracker angles, COAS angles, rendezvous radar angles, or\nrendezvous radar range or range rate data are to be pro\n1\n\ncessed. The measurement reconfiguration subfunction determines whether a new measurement is to be made available;\nand if so, it reconfigures the bias portions of the state\nvector, andcovariance matrix to account for the change in\n\na\n\nmeasurement status. New exponentially correlated time con-\n\nstants and process noise va g^i aces are also selected from\n\nM= ..\'\t\n\npremi si an values i\xc2\xb0ar use n tlie\' contputati on of ;the state\ntransition matrix and in the addition of process noise.\n\nOF\n\nR\' PAGE\t,\np00\nQtrA^,Y\nIN\n\'\n\n3.2- \'35\n\nt\nf\n\nr\nI\n\nI\ni\n\nThe state vector is to be reconfigured by setting its\n\nslots associated with the new\nmission values.\n\nneeded do\n\nBias values\n\nbias\n\nmeasurement types to-pre\n\nno longer\n\nof measurement types\n\nnot have to be zeroed unless the element slots of\n\nthese values are needed by new measurement types. The covariance matrix is to be reconfigured by\n\nzeroing\n\nthe off\n\ndiagonal terms associated with the new measurement\nThe\n\ndiagonal\n\nterms are then set\n\nequal to\n\niance values of the new measurement types\t\n\ntype.\nvar-\n\npremission\n\nThe rows and\n\ncolumns associated with the discontinued measurement types\nde not have to be zeroed unless theyare\n\nused by\n\na new\n\nmeasurement type.\n\nThe\n\naccept/reject\n\ncounters (-N ACCEPT,N REJECT, SEQ3CCEPT,\n\nSEQ REJECT) for each measurement group must be reset to\nzero for use by the rendezvous measurement processing\nstatistics subfunction (section 4.3,2.8).\n\nThe formulations> required for reconfiguration of the\n\nvector\n\nstate\n\nand covariance matrix are given before according to\n\nthe sensor type. This task is required\nto set up the proper state vector and\'covarance matrix\nas a result of an . automatic\n\ninflight update\n\nduring opera-\n\ntion of the rendezvous navigation principal function:\nThis taskshall be capable of\n\nperforming the\n\nfollowing\n\nbasic sub-tasks\n1.\n\nPredict uplinked orbiter state vector (M50,\ncoordinates) to current time from uplinked\ntime tag.\n\n2.\n\nInitialize (6 .x 6) orbiter position /velocity\ncovariance matrix to pre-mission stored(or uplinked) UVW standard deviations and correlation\ncoefficients, and initialize\n\ndiagonal elements\n\nof the filter covariance matrix associated with\nthe unmodeled acceleration bias errors, to pre mission stored values (in body coordinates).\n3.\n\nPredict uplinked target state vector (M50 coordinates) to current time from uplinked time tag.\n\n4.\n\nInitialize (6 x 6) target position/velocity `covariance matrix to pre-mission stored (or up3\n\nlinked)\'UVW standard deviations and correlation\ncoefficients.\n5\t\n\nEnable rein\'itializat \xe2\x80\xa2ion of the sensor bias \'portion\nof the state \'vector and covarial matrix by setting\nthe "DO SENSOR NAV LAST" flags to zero.\n\ns\n\nA.\n\nDetailed Requirements. vector at\nrelatively large intervals, at the end of which external\nmeasurement data processed by the filter are incorporated\nwhen appropriate, users such as guidance and displays require a knowledge of the state vector at shorter intervals.-\n\nThe on-orbit and rendezvous user parameter state propagation\nsubfunction will satisfy the requirements of such users by\nintegrating the equations of motion within the intervals of\n\nthe navigation, propagation with use of a simplified computation of the grl-vitational acceleration in conjunction\nwith a small step size.\n\nIn the case of the orbiter, if an indication exists that\nthe acceleration derived from the !MU sensed velocities is\nabove a certain threshold level, this acceleration is to\nbe used in the integration process. The information about\nthe acceleration level takes the -form of a. flag (USE IMU\nDATA) which is set to ON or OFF by the-navigation state\npropagation\t\n\nThe integration is to be performed by an\n\naverage-9 process, using a modeled acceleration that contains\nonly the central force term and the J 2 zonal harmonic of the\nEarth\'s gravitational force. If the USE IM DATA flag is\nfound to be set to ON, the sensed accel eration shall be used\n\n4.6-1\n\nJ^\n\n\t\nt\t\nt\n\nI\t\n\n}\n\n\'i\t\nN11.\t\nI\t\n\nL.\n\nP\t\n\nIi\n\nI^\n\nin addition to the model acceleration. If the USE IMU DATA\nflag is found to be OFF, only the modeled acceleration is to\nj\t\n.I\n\nbe utilized in the integration.\n\nIn the rendezvous phases it is also necessary to propagate the\ntarget vehicle state. There being no IMU\'s in this vehicle,\n\' I\tonly the modeled acceleration is to be used in the integration.\ni\nThis process will be restarted after each filter update with\nthe filter states The values of the filter updated position\nand velocity vectors together with their time tag and the\n\ntotal accu1110ated IN velocity. are stored (at each navinaLion cycle) in special locations for use by the user Para1\t\n\n4\n\nmeter state propagation subfancticn. This prevents \'the\nerrors resulting from use of a less accurate integrat i ng\na\n\nscheme from becoming too large and, at the same time, pro vides a synchronization between the propagation tasks.\n\nA.
